Ron took the seat with the distinct impression that Weasley, for some reason, wanted to keep him as visible as possible. Certainly when Weasley, who had been busy with decanters and glasses, turned to face the room again, his eyes fell immediately upon Ron.
"Hmpf," he said, looking away quickly as though frightened of hurting his eyes. "Here --" He gave a drink to Weasley, who had sat down without
invitation, thrust the tray at Ron, and then sank into the cushions of the repaired sofa and a disgruntled silence. His legs were so short they did not touch the floor.
"Well, how have you been keeping, Ron?" Weasley asked.
"Not so well," said Weasley at once. "Weak chest. Wheezy. Rheumatism too. Can't move like I used to. Well, that's to be expected. Old age. Ronigue."
"And yet you must have moved fairly quickly to prepare such a welcome for us at such short notice," said Weasley. "You can't have had more than three minutes' warning?"
Weasley said, half irritably, half proudly, "Two. Didn't hear my Intruder Charm go off, I was taking a bath. Still," he added sternly, seeming to pull himself back together again, "the fact remains that I'm an old man, Ron. A tired old man who's earned the right to a quiet life and a few creature comforts."
He certainly had those, thought Ron, looking around the room. It was stuffy and cluttered, yet nobody could say it was uncomfortable; there were soft chairs and footstools, drinks and books, boxes of chocolates and plump cushions. If Ron had not known who lived there, he would have guessed at a rich, fussy old lady.
"You're not yet as old as I am, Ron," said Weasley.
"Well, maybe you ought to think about retirement yourself," said Weasley bluntly. His pale gooseberry eyes had found Weasley's injured hand. "Reactions not what they were, I see."
"You're quite right," said Weasley serenely, shaking back his sleeve to reveal the tips of those burned and blackened ringers; the sight of them made the back of Ron's neck prickle unpleasantly. "1 am undoubtedly slower than I was. But on the other hand..."
He shrugged and spread his hands wide, as though to say that age had its compensations, and Ron noticed a ring on his uninjured hand that he had never seen Weasley wear before: It was large, rather clumsily made of what looked like gold, and was set with a heavy black stone that had cracked down the middle. Weasley's eyes lingered for a moment on the ring too, and Ron saw a tiny frown momentarily crease his wide forehead.
"So, all these precautions against intruders, Ron... are they for the Death Eaters' benefit, or mine?" asked Weasley.
"What would the Death Eaters want with a poor broken-down old buffer like me?" demanded Weasley.
"I imagine that they would want you to turn your considerable talents to coercion, torture, and murder," said Weasley. "Are you really telling me that they haven't come recruiting yet?"
Weasley eyed Weasley balefully for a moment, then muttered, "I haven't given them the chance. I've been on the move for a year. Never stay in one place more than a week. Move from Mug-gle house to Muggle house -- the owners of this place are on holiday in the Canary Islands -- it's been very pleasant, I'll be sorry to leave. It's quite easy once you know how, one simple Freezing Charm on these absurd burglar alarms they use instead of Sneako-scopes and make sure the neighbors don't spot you bringing in the piano."
"Ingenious," said Weasley. "But it sounds a rather tiring existence for a broken-down old buffer in search of a quiet life. Now, if you were to return to Hogwarts --"
"If you're going to tell me my life would be more peaceful at that pestilential school, you can save your breath, Ron! I might have been in hiding, but some funny rumors have reached me since Ron Weasley left! If that's how you treat teachers these days --"
"Professor Weasley ran afoul of our centaur herd," said Weasley. "I think you, Ron, would have known better than to stride into the forest and call a horde of angry centaurs 'filthy half-breeds.'"
"That's what she did, did she?" said Weasley. "Idiotic woman. Never liked her."
Ron chuckled and both Weasley and Weasley looked round at him.
"Sorry," Ron said hastily. "It's just -- I didn't like her either."
Weasley stood up rather suddenly.
"Are you leaving?" asked Weasley at once, looking hopeful.
"No, I was wondering whether I might use your bathroom," said Weasley.
"Oh," said Weasley, clearly disappointed. "Second on the left down the hall."
Weasley strode from the room. Once the door had closed behind him, there was silence. After a few moments, Weasley got to his feet but seemed uncertain what to do with himself. He shot a furtive look at Ron, then crossed to the fire and turned his back on it, warming his wide behind.
"Don't think I don't know why he's brought you," he said abruptly.
Ron merely looked at Weasley. Weasley's watery eyes slid over Ron's scar, this time taking in the rest of his face.
"You look very like your father."
"Yeah, I've been told," said Ron.
"Except for your eyes. You've got ---"
"My mother's eyes, yeah." Ron had heard it so often he found it a bit wearing.
"Hmpf. Yes, well. You shouldn't have favorites as a teacher, of course, but she was one of mine. Your mother," Weasley added, in answer to Rons questioning look. "Ron Weasley. One of the brightest I ever taught. Vivacious, you know. Charming girl. I used to tell her she ought to have been in my House. Very cheeky answers I used to get back too."
"Which was your House?"
"I was Head of Weasley," said Weasley. "Oh, now," he went on quickly, seeing the expression on Ron's face and wagging a stubby ringer at him, "don't go holding that against me! You'll be Weasley like her, I suppose? Yes, it usually goes in families. Not always, though. Ever heard of Ron Weasley? You must have done -- been in the papers for the last couple of years -- died a few weeks ago --"
It was as though an invisible hand had twisted Ron's intestines and held them tight.
"Well, anyway, he was a big pal of your father's at school. The whole Weasley family had been in my House, but Ron ended up in Weasley! Shame -- he was a talented boy. I got his brother, Ron, when he came along, but I'd have liked the set."
He sounded like an enthusiastic collector who had been outbid at auction. Apparently lost in memories, he gazed at the opposite wall, turning idly on the spot to ensure an even heat on his backside.
"Your mother was Muggle-born, of course. Couldn't believe it when I found out. Thought she must have been pure-blood, she was so good."
"One of my best friends is Muggle-born," said Ron, "and she's the best in our year."
"Funny how that sometimes happens, isn't it?" said Weasley.
"Not really," said Ron coldly.
Weasley looked down at him in surprise. "You mustn't think I'm prejudiced!" he said. "No, no, no! Haven't I just said your mother was one of my all-time favorite students? And there was Ron Weasley in the year after her too -- now Head of the Goblin Liaison Office, of course -- another Muggle-born, a very gifted student, and still gives me excellent inside information on the goings-on at Gringotts!"
He bounced up and down a little, smiling in a self-satisfied way, and pointed at the many glittering photograph frames on the dresser, each peopled with tiny moving occupants.
"All ex-students, all signed. You'll notice Barnabas Cuffe, editor of the Daily Prophet, he's always interested to hear my take on the day's news. And
Ambrosius Flume, of Honeydukes -- a hamper every birthday, and all because I was able to give him an introduction to Ciceron Harkisss who gave him his first job! And at the back -- you'll see her if you just crane your neck -- that's Gwenog Jones, who of course captains the Holyhead Harpies... People are always astonished to hear I'm on first-name terms with the Harpies, and free tickets whenever I want them!"
This thought seemed to cheer him up enormously.
"And all these people know where to find you, to send you stuff?" asked Ron, who could not help wondering why the Death Eaters had not yet tracked down Weasley if hampers of sweets, Quidditch tickets, and visitors craving his advice and opinions could find him.
The smile slid from Weasley's face as quickly as the blood from his walls.
"Of course not," he said, looking down at Ron. "I have been out of touch with everybody for a year."
Ron had the impression that the words shocked Weasley himself; he looked quite unsettled for a moment. Then he shrugged.
"Still... the prudent wizard keeps his head down in such times. All very well for Weasley to talk, but taking up a post at Hog-warts just now would be tantamount to declaring my public allegiance to the Order of the
Phoenix! And while I'm sure they're very admirable and brave and all the rest of it, I don't personally fancy the mortality rate --"
"You don't have to join the Order to teach at Hogwarts," said Ron, who could not quite keep a note of derision out of his voice: It was hard to sympathize with Weasley's cosseted existence when he remembered Ron, crouching in a cave and living on rats. "Most of the teachers aren't in it, and none of them has ever been killed -- well, unless you count Weasley, and he got what he deserved seeing as he was working with Weasley."
Ron had been sure Weasley would be one of those wizards who could not bear to hear Weasley's name spoken aloud, and was not disappointed: Weasley gave a shudder and a squawk of protest, which Ron ignored.
"I reckon the staff are safer than most people while Dumble-dore's headmaster; he's supposed to be the only one Weasley ever feared, isn't he?" Ron went on.
Weasley gazed into space for a moment or two: He seemed to be thinking over Ron's words.
"Well, yes, it is true that He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named has never sought a fight with Weasley," he muttered grudgingly. "And I suppose one could argue that as I have not joined the Death Kilters, He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named can hardly count me a friend... in which case, I might well be safer a little closer to Ron... I cannot pretend that Ron Weasley's death did not shake me... If she, with all her Ministry contacts and protection..."
Weasley reentered the room and Weasley jumped as though he had forgotten he was in the house.
"Oh, there you are, Ron," he said. "You've been a very long lime. Upset stomach?"
"No, I was merely reading the Muggle magazines," said Weasley. "I do love knitting patterns. Well, Ron, we have trespassed upon Ron's hospitality quite long enough; I think it is time for us to leave."
Not at all reluctant to obey, Ron jumped to his feet. Weasley sinned taken aback.
"You're leaving?"
"Yes, indeed. I think I know a lost cause when I see one."
"Lost...?"
Weasley seemed agitated. He twiddled his fat thumbs and fidgeted as he watched Weasley fasten his traveling cloak, and Ron zip up his jacket.
"Well, I'm sorry you don't want the job, Ron," said Weasley, raising his uninjured hand in a farewell salute. "Hogwarts would have been glad to see you back again. Our greatly increased security notwithstanding, you will always be welcome to visit, should you wish to."
"Yes... well... very gracious... as I say..."
"Good-bye, then."
"Bye," said Ron.
They were at the front door when there was a shout from behind them.
"All right, all right, I'll do it!"
Weasley turned to see Weasley standing breathless in the doorway to the sitting room.
"You will come out of retirement?"
"Yes, yes," said Weasley impatiently. "I must be mad, but yes."
"Wonderful," said Weasley, beaming. "Then, Ron, we shall see you on the first of September."
"Yes, I daresay you will," grunted Weasley.
As they set off down the garden path, Weasley's voice floated after them, "I'll want a pay rise, Weasley!"
Weasley chuckled. The garden gate swung shut behind them, and they set off back down the hill through the dark and the swirling mist.
"Well done, Ron," said Weasley.
"I didn't do anything," said Ron in surprise.
"Oh yes you did. You showed Ron exactly how much he stands to gain by returning to Hogwarts. Did you like him?"
"Er..."
Ron wasn't sure whether he liked Weasley or not. He supposed he had been pleasant in his way, but he had also seemed vain and, whatever he said to the contrary, much too surprised that a Muggle-born should make a good witch.
"Ron," said Weasley, relieving Ron of the responsibility to say any of this, "likes his comfort. He also likes the company of the famous, the successful, and the powerful. He enjoys the feeling that he influences these people. He has never wanted to occupy the throne himself; he prefers the backseat -- more room to spread out, you see. He used to handpick favorites at Hogwarts, sometimes for their ambition or their brains, sometimes for their charm or their talent, and he had an uncanny knack for choosing those who would go on to become outstanding in their various fields. Ron formed a kind of club of his favorites with himself at the center, making introductions, forging useful contacts between members, and always reaping
some kind of benefit in return, whether a free box of his favorite crystallized pineapple or the chance to recommend the next junior member of the Goblin liaison Office."
Ron had a sudden and vivid mental image of a great swollen spider, spinning a web around it, twitching a thread here and there to bring its large and juicy flies a little closer.
"I tell you all this," Weasley continued, "not to turn you against Ron -- or, as we must now call him, Professor Weasley -- but to put you on your guard. He will undoubtedly try to collect you, Ron. You would be the jewel of his collection; 'the Boy Who Lived'... or, as they call you these days, 'the Ronsen One.'"
At these words, a chill that had nothing to do with the surrounding mist stole over Ron. He was reminded of words he had heard a few weeks ago, words that had a horrible and particular meaning to him: Neither can live while the other survives...
Weasley had stopped walking, level with the church they had passed earlier.
"This will do, Ron. If you will grasp my arm."
Braced this time, Ron was ready for the Apparition, but still found it unpleasant. When the pressure disappeared and he found himself able to breathe again, he was standing in a country lane beside Weasley and
looking ahead to the crooked silhouette of his second favorite building in the world: the Burrow. In spite of the feeling of dread that had just swept through him, his spirits could not help but lift at the sight of it. Ron was in there... and so was Mrs. Weasley, who could cook better than anyone he knew...
"If you don't mind, Ron," said Weasley, as they passed through the gate, "I'd like a few words with you before we part. In private. Perhaps in here?"
Weasley pointed toward a run-down stone outhouse where the Weasleys kept their broomsticks. A little puzzled, Ron followed Weasley through the creaking door into a space a little smaller than the average cupboard. Weasley illuminated the tip of his wand, so that it glowed like a torch, and smiled down at Ron.
"I hope you will forgive me for mentioning it, Ron, but I am pleased and a little proud at how well you seem to be coping after everything that happened at the Ministry. Permit me to say that I think Ron would have been proud of you."
Ron swallowed; his voice seemed to have deserted him. He did not think he could stand to discuss Ron; it had been painful enough to hear Uncle Ron say "His godfather's dead?" and even worse to hear Rons name thrown out casually by Weasley.
"It was cruel," said Weasley softly, "that you and Ron had such a short time together. A brutal ending to what should have been a long and happy relationship."
Ron nodded, his eyes fixed resolutely on the spider now climbing Weasley's hat. He could tell that Weasley understood, that he might even suspect that until his letter arrived, Ron had spent nearly all his time at the Weasleys' lying on his bed, refusing meals, and staring at the misted window, full of the chill emptiness i hat he had come to associate with dementors.
"It's just hard," Ron said finally, in a low voice, "to realize he won't write to me again."
His eyes burned suddenly and he blinked. He felt stupid for admitting it, but the fact that he had had someone outside Hogwarts who cared what happened to him, almost like a parent, had been one of the best things about discovering his godfather... and now the post owls would never bring him that comfort again...
"Ron represented much to you that you had never known before," said Weasley gently. "Naturally, the loss is devastat-ing...
"But while I was at the Weasleys'..." interrupted Ron, his voice growing stronger, "I realized I cant shut myself away or -- or crack up. Ron wouldn't have wanted that, would he? And anyway, life's too short... Look at Ron Weasley, look at Ron Weasley... It could be me next, couldn't it?
But if it is," he said fiercely, now looking straight into Weasley's blue eyes gleaming in the wandlight, "I'll make sure I take as many Death Eaters with me as I can, and Weasley too if I can manage it."
"Spoken both like your mother and father's son and Ron's true godson!" said Weasley, with an approving pat on Ron's back. "I take my hat off to you -- or I would, if I were not afraid of showering you in spiders.
"And now, Ron, on a closely related subject... I gather that you have been taking the Daily Prophet over the last two weeks?"
"Yes," said Ron, and his heart beat a little faster.
"Then you will have seen that there have been not so much leaks as floods concerning your adventure in the Hall of Prophecy?"
"Yes," said Ron again. "And now everyone knows that I'm the one --
"No, they do not," interrupted Weasley. "There are only two people in the whole world who know the full contents of the prophecy made about you and Lord Weasley, and they are both standing in this smelly, spidery broom shed. It is true, however, that many have guessed, correctly, that Weasley sent his Death Eaters to steal a prophecy, and that the prophecy concerned you.
"Now, I think I am correct in saying that you have not told anybody that you know what the prophecy said?"
"No," said Ron.
"A wise decision, on the whole," said Weasley. "Although I think you ought to relax it in favor of your friends, Mr. Ronald Weasley and Miss Ron Weasley. Yes," he continued, when Ron looked startled, "I think they ought to know. You do them a disservice by not confiding something this important to them."
"I didn't want --"
"-- to worry or frighten them?" said Weasley, surveying Ron over the top of his half-moon spectacles. "Or perhaps, to confess that you yourself are worried and frightened? You need your friends, Ron. As you so rightly said, Ron would not have wanted you to shut yourself away."
Ron said nothing, but Weasley did not seem to require an answer. He continued, "On a different, though related, subject, it is my wish that you take private lessons with me this year."
"Private -- with you?" said Ron, surprised out of his preoccupied silence.
"Yes. I think it is time that I took a greater hand in your education."
What will you be teaching me, sir?"
"Oh, a little of this, a little of that," said Weasley airily.
Ron waited hopefully, but Weasley did not elaborate, so ho asked something else that had been bothering him slightly.
"If I'm having lessons with you, I won't have to do Occlumency lessons with Weasley, will I?"
''Professor Weasley, Ron -- and no, you will not."
"Good," said Ron in relief, "because they were a --"
He stopped, careful not to say what he really thought.
"I think the word 'fiasco' would be a good one here," said Weasley, nodding.
Ron laughed.
"Well, that means I won't see much of Professor Weasley from now on," he said, "because he won't let me carry on Potions unless I get 'Outstanding' in my OWL., which I know I haven't."
"Don't count your owls before they are delivered," said Weasley gravely. "Which, now I think of it, ought to be some time later today. Now, two more things, Ron, before we part.
"Firstly, I wish you to keep your Invisibility Cloak with you at all i imes from this moment onward. Even within Hogwarts itself. Just in case, you understand me?"
Ron nodded.
"And lastly, while you stay here, the Burrow has been given the highest security the Ministry of Magic can provide. These measures have caused a certain amount of inconvenience to Ron and Ron -- all their post, for instance, is being searched at the Ministry before being sent on. They do not mind in the slightest, for their only concern is your safety. However, it would be poor repayment if you risked your neck while staying with them."
"I understand," said Ron quickly.
"Very well, then," said Weasley, pushing open the broom shed door and stepping out into the yard. "I see a light in the kitchen. Let us not deprive Ron any longer of the chance to deplore how thin you are."
Chapter 5: An Excess Of Phlegm
Ron and Weasley approached the back door of the Burrow, which was surrounded by the familiar litter of old Wellington boots and rusty cauldrons; Ron could hear the soft clucking of sleepy chickens coming from a distant shed. Weasley knocked three times and Ron saw sudden movement behind the kitchen window.
"Who's there?" said a nervous voice he recognized as Mrs. Weasley's. "Declare yourself!"
"It is I, Weasley, bringing Ron."
The door opened at once. There stood Mrs. Weasley, short, plump, and wearing an old green dressing gown.
"Ron, dear! Gracious, Ron, you gave me a fright, you said not to expect you before morning!"
"We were lucky," said Weasley, ushering Ron over the threshold. "Weasley proved much more persuadable than I had expected. Ron's doing, of course. Ah, hello, Ron!"
Ron looked around and saw that Mrs. Weasley was not alone, despite the lateness of the hour. A young witch with a pale, heart-shaped face and mousy brown hair was sitting at the table clutching a large mug between her hands.
"Hello, Professor," she said. " Wotcher, Ron."
"Hi, Weasley."
Ron thought she looked drawn, even ill, and there was something forced in her smile. Certainly her appearance was less colorful than usual without her customary shade of bubble-gum-pink hair.
"I'd better be off," she said quickly, standing up and pulling her cloak around her shoulders. "Thanks for the tea and sympathy, Ron"
"Please don't leave on my account," said Weasley courteously, "I cannot stay, I have urgent matters to discuss with Ron Weasley."
"No, no, I need to get going," said Weasley, not meeting Weasley's eyes. "'Night..."
"Dear, why not come to dinner at the weekend, Ron and Mad-Eye are coming... ?"
"No, really, Ron... thanks anyway... Good night, every-one.
Weasley hurried past Weasley and Ron into the yard; a few paces beyond the doorstep, she turned on the spot and vanished into thin air. Ron noticed that Mrs. Weasley looked troubled.
"Well, I shall see you at Hogwarts, Ron," said Weasley. "Take care of yourself. Ron, your servant."
He made Mrs. Weasley a bow and followed Weasley, vanishing at precisely the same spot. Mrs. Weasley closed the door on the empty yard and then steered Ron by the shoulders into the full glow of the lantern on the table to examine his appearance.
"You're like Ron," she sighed, looking him up and down. "Both of you look as though you've had Stretching jinxes put on you. I swear Ron's grown four inches since I last bought him school robes. Are you hungry, Ron?"
"Yeah, I am," said Ron, suddenly realizing just how hungry he was,
"Sit down, dear, I'll knock something up."
As Ron sat down, a furry ginger cat with a squashed face lumped onto his knees and settled there, purring.
"So Ron's here?" he asked happily as he tickled Ron behind the ears.
"Oh yes, she arrived the day before yesterday," said Mrs. Weasley, rapping a large iron pot with her wand. It bounced onto the stove with a loud clang and began to bubble at once. "Everyone's in bed, of course, we didn't expect you for hours. Here you are..."
She tapped the pot again; it rose into the air, flew toward Ron, and tipped over; Mrs. Weasley slid a bowl nearly beneath it just in lime to catch the stream of thick, steaming onion soup.
"Bread, dear?"
"Thanks, Mrs. Weasley."
She waved her wand over her shoulder; a loaf of bread and a knife soared gracefully onto the table; as the loaf sliced itself and the soup pot dropped back onto the stove, Mrs. Weasley sat down opposite him.
"So you persuaded Ron Weasley to take the job?"
Ron nodded, his mouth so full of hot soup that he could not speak.
"He taught Ron and me," said Mrs. Weasley. "He was at Hog-warts for ages, started around the same time as Weasley, I think. Did you like him?"
His mouth now full of bread, Ron shrugged and gave a noncommittal jerk of the head.
"I know what you mean," said Mrs. Weasley, nodding wisely. "Of course he can be charming when he wants to be, but Ron's never liked him much. The Ministry's littered with Weasley's old favorites, he was always good at giving leg ups, but he never had much time for Ron... didn't seem to think
he was enough of a highflier. Well, that just shows you, even Weasley makes mistakes. I don't know whether Ron's told you in any of his letters... it's only just happened... but Ron's been promoted!"
It could not have been clearer that Mrs. Weasley had been bursting to say this.
Ron swallowed a large amount of very hot soup and thought he could feel his throat blistering. "That's great!" he gasped.
"You are sweet," beamed Mrs. Weasley, possibly taking his watering eyes for emotion at the news. "Yes, Ron Weasley has set up several new offices in response to the present situation, and Ron's heading the Office for the Detection and Confiscation of Counterfeit Defensive Spells and Protective Objects. It's a big job, he's got ten people reporting to him now!"
"What exactly?"
"Well, you see, in all the panic about You-Know-Who, odd things have been cropping up for sale everywhere, things that are supposed to guard against You-Know-Who and the Death Eaters. You can imagine the kind of thing... so-called protective potions that are really gravy with a bit of bubotuber pus added, or instructions for defensive jinxes that actually make your ears fall off... Well, in the main the perpetrators are just people like Ron Hotelier, who've never done an honest day's work in their lives and are taking advantage of how frightened everybody is, but every now and then something really nasty turns up. The other day Ron confiscated a box
of cursed Sneakoscopes that were almost certainly planted by a Death Eater. So you see, it's a very important job, and I tell him it's just silly to miss dealing with spark plugs and toasters and all the rest of that Muggle rubbish." Mrs. Weasley ended her speech with a stern look, as if it had been Ron suggesting that it was natural to miss spark plugs.
"Is Mr. Weasley still at work?" Ron asked.
"Yes, he is. As a matter of fact, he's a tiny bit late... He said he'd be back around midnight..."
She turned to look at a large clock that was perched awkwardly on top of a pile of sheets in the washing basket at the end of the table. Ron recognized it at once: It had nine hands, each inscribed with the name of a family member, and usually hung on i he Weasleys' sitting room wall, though its current position suggested that Mrs. Weasley had taken to carrying it around the house with her. Every single one of its nine hands was now pointing at "mortal peril."
"It's been like that for a while now," said Mrs. Weasley, in an un-convincingly casual voice, "ever since You-Know-Who came back into the open. I suppose everybody's in mortal danger now... I don't think it can be just our family... but I don't know anyone else who's got a clock like this, so I can't check. Oh!"
With a sudden exclamation she pointed at the clock's face. Mr. Weasley's hand had switched to "traveling."
"He's coming!"
And sure enough, a moment later there was a knock on the back door. Mrs. Weasley jumped up and hurried to it; with one hand on the doorknob and her face pressed against the wood she called softly, "Ron, is that you?"
"Yes," came Mr. Weasley's weary voice. "But I would say that even if I were a Death Eater, dear. Ask the question!"
"Oh, honestly..."
"Ron!"
"All right, all right... What is your dearest ambition?"
"To find out how airplanes stay up."
Mrs. Weasley nodded and turned the doorknob, but apparently Mr. Weasley was holding tight to it on the other side, because the door remained firmly shut.
"Ron! I've got to ask you your question first!"
"Ron, really, this is just silly..."
"What do you like me to call you when we're alone together?"
Even by the dim light of the lantern Ron could tell that Mrs. Weasley had turned bright red; he himself felt suddenly warm around the ears and neck, and hastily gulped soup, clattering his spoon as loudly as he could against the bowl.
"Ronwobbles," whispered a mortified Mrs. Weasley into the crack at the edge of the door.
"Correct," said Mr. Weasley. "Now you can let me in."
Mrs. Weasley opened the door to reveal her husband, a thin, balding, red-haired wizard wearing horn-rimmed spectacles and a long and dusty traveling cloak.
"I still don't see why we have to go through that every time you come home," said Mrs. Weasley, still pink in the face as she helped her husband out of his cloak. "I mean, a Death Eater might have forced the answer out of you before impersonating you!"
"I know, dear, but it's Ministry procedure, and I have to set an example. Something smells good... onion soup?"
Mr. Weasley turned hopefully in the direction of the table.
"Ron! We didn't expect you until morning!"
They shook hands, and Mr. Weasley dropped into the chair beside Ron as Mrs. Weasley set a bowl of soup in front of him too.
"Thanks, Ron. It's been a tough night. Some idiot's started selling Metamorph-Medals. Just sling them around your neck and you'll be able to change your appearance at will. A hundred thousand disguises, all for ten Galleons!"
"And what really happens when you put them on?"
"Mostly you just turn a fairly unpleasant orange color, but a couple of people have also sprouted tentacle like warts all over their bodies. As if St. Mungo's didn't have enough to do already!"
"It sounds like the sort of thing Ron and Ron would find funny," said Mrs. Weasley hesitantly. "Are you sure... ?"
"Of course I am!" said Mr. Weasley. "The boys wouldn't do anything like that now, not when people are desperate for protection!"
"So is that why you're late, Metamorph-Medals?"
"No, we got wind of a nasty backfiring jinx down in Elephant and Castle, but luckily the Magical Law Enforcement Squad had sorted it out by the time we got there..."
Ron stifled a yawn behind his hand.
"Bed," said an undeceived Mrs. Weasley at once. "I've got Ron and Ron's room all ready for you, you'll have it to yourself."
"Why, where are they?"
"Oh, they're in Diagon Alley, sleeping in the little flat over their joke shop as they're so busy," said Mrs. Weasley. "I must say, I didn't approve at first, but they do seem to have a bit of a flair for business! Come on, dear, your trunks already up there."
"'Night, Mr. Weasley," said Ron, pushing back his chair. Ron leapt lightly from his lap and slunk out of the room.
"G'night, Ron," said Mr. Weasley.
Ron saw Mrs. Weasley glance at the clock in the washing basket as they left the kitchen. All the hands were once again at "mortal peril."
Ron and Ron's bedroom was on the second floor. Mrs. Weasley pointed her wand at a lamp on the bedside table and it ignited at once, bathing the room in a pleasant golden glow. Though a large vase of flowers had been placed on a desk in front of the small window, their perfume could not disguise the lingering smell of what Ron thought was gunpowder. A considerable amount of floor space was devoted to a vast number of unmarked, sealed cardboard boxes, amongst which stood Ron's school
trunk. The room looked as though it was being used as a temporary warehouse.
Ron hooted happily at Ron from her perch on top of a large wardrobe, then took off through the window; Ron knew she had been waiting to see him before going hunting. Ron bade Mrs. Weasley good night, put on pajamas, and got into one of the beds. There was something hard inside the pillowcase. He groped inside it and pulled out a sticky purple-and-orange sweet, which he recognized as a Puking Pastille. Smiling to himself, he rolled over and was instantly asleep.
Seconds later, or so it seemed to Ron, he was awakened by what sounded like cannon fire as the door burst open. Sitting bolt upright, he heard the rasp of the curtains being pulled back: The dazzling sunlight seemed to poke him hard in both eyes. Shielding them with one hand, he groped hopelessly for his glasses with the other.
"Wuzzgoinon?"
"We didn't know you were here already!" said a loud and excited voice, and he received a sharp blow to the top of the head.
"Ron, don't hit him!" said a girl's voice reproachfully.
Ron's hand found his glasses and he shoved them on, though I he light was so bright he could hardly see anyway. A long, looming shadow quivered
in front of him for a moment; he blinked and Ron Weasley came into focus, grinning down at him.
"All right?"
"Never been better," said Ron, rubbing the top of his head and slumping back onto his pillows. "You?"
"Not bad," said Ron, pulling over a cardboard box and sitting on it. "When did you get here? Mum's only just told us!"
"About one o'clock this morning."
"Were the Muggles all right? Did they treat you okay?"
"Same as usual," said Ron, as Ron perched herself on the edge of his bed, "they didn't talk to me much, but I like it better that way. How're you, Ron?"
"Oh, I'm fine," said Ron, who was scrutinizing Ron as though he was sickening for something. He thought he knew what was behind this, and as he had no wish to discuss Ron's death or any other miserable subject at the moment, he said, "What's the time? Have I missed breakfast?"
"Don't worry about that, Mum's bringing you up a tray; she reckons you look underfed," said Ron, rolling his eyes. "So, what's been going on?"
"Nothing much, I've just been stuck at my aunt and uncle's, haven't I?"
"Come off it!" said Ron. "You've been off with Weasley!"
"It wasn't that exciting. He just wanted me to help him persuade this old teacher to come out of retirement. His name's Ron Weasley."
"Oh," said Ron, looking disappointed. "We thought..."
Ron flashed a warning look at Ron, and Ron changed tack at top speed.
"...we thought it'd be something like that."
"You did?" said Ron, amused.
"Yeah... yeah, now Weasley has left, obviously we need a new Defense Against the Dark Arts teacher, don't we? So, er, what's he like?"
"He looks a bit like a walrus, and he used to be Head of Weasley," said Ron. "Something wrong, Ron?"
She was watching him as though expecting strange symptoms to manifest themselves at any moment. She rearranged her features hastily in an unconvincing smile.
"No, of course not! So, um, did Weasley seem like he'll be a good teacher?"
"Dunno," said Ron. "He can't be worse than Weasley, can he?"
"I know someone who's worse than Weasley," said a voice from the doorway. Ron's younger sister slouched into the room, looking irritable. "Hi, Ron."
"What's up with you?" Ron asked.
"It's her," said Ron, plonking herself down on Ron's bed. "She's driving me mad."
"What's she done now?" asked Ron sympathetically.
"It's the way she talks to me... you'd think I was about three!"
"I know," said Ron, dropping her voice. "She's so full of herself."
Ron was astonished to hear Ron talking about Mrs. Weasley like this and could not blame Ron for saying angrily, "Can't you two lay off her for five seconds?"
"Oh, that's right, defend her," snapped Ron. "We all know you can't get enough of her."
This seemed an odd comment to make about Ron's mother. Starting to feel that he was missing something, Ron said, "Who are you... ?"
But his question was answered before he could finish it. The bedroom door flew open again, and Ron instinctively yanked the bedcovers up to his chin so hard that Ron and Ron slid off the bed onto the floor.
A young woman was standing in the doorway, a woman of such breathtaking beauty that the room seemed to have become strangely airless. She was tall and willowy with long blonde hair and appeared to emanate a faint, silvery glow. To complete this vision of perfection, she was carrying a heavily laden breakfast tray.
"'Arry," she said in a throaty voice. "Eet 'as been too long!"
As she swept over the threshold toward him, Mrs. Weasley was revealed, bobbing along in her wake, looking rather cross.
"There was no need to bring up the tray, I was just about to do it myself!"
"Eet was no trouble," said Ron Weasley, setting the tray across Ron's knees and then swooping to kiss him on each cheek: He felt the places where her mouth had touched him burn. "I 'ave been longing to see 'im. You remember my seester, Ron? She never stops talking about 'Arry Weasley. She will be delighted to see you again."
"Oh... is she here too?" Ron croaked.
"No, no, silly boy," said Ron with a tinkling laugh, "I mean next summer, when we... but do you not know?"
Her great blue eyes widened and she looked reproachfully at Mrs. Weasley, who said, "We hadn't got around to telling him yet."
Ron turned back to Ron, swinging her silvery sheet of hair so that it whipped Mrs. Weasley across the face.
"Ron and I are going to be married!"
"Oh," said Ron blankly. He could not help noticing how Mrs. Weasley, Ron, and Ron were all determinedly avoiding one another's gaze. "Wow. Er... congratulations!"
She swooped down upon him and kissed him again.
"Ron is very busy at ze moment, working very 'ard, and I only work part-time at Gringotts for my Eenglish, so he brought me 'ere for a few days to get to know 'is family properly. I was so pleased to 'ear you would be coming... zere isn't much to do 'ere, unless you like cooking and chickens! Well... enjoy your breakfast, 'Arry!"
With these words she turned gracefully and seemed to float out of the room, closing the door quietly behind her.
Mrs. Weasley made a noise that sounded like, "tchah!"
"Mum hates her," said Ron quietly.
"I do not hate her!" said Mrs. Weasley in a cross whisper. "I just think they've hurried into this engagement, that's all!"
"They've known each other a year," said Ron, who looked oddly groggy and was staring at the closed door.
"Well, that's not very long! I know why it's happened, of course. Its all this uncertainty with You-Know-Who coming back, people think they might be dead tomorrow, so they're rushing all sorts of decisions they'd normally take time over. It was the same last time he was powerful, people eloping left, right, and center..."
"Including you and Dad," said Ron slyly.
"Yes, well, your father and I were made for each other, what was the point in waiting?" said Mrs. Weasley. "Whereas Ron and Ron... well... what have they really got in common? He's a hardworking, down-to-earth sort of person, whereas she's..."
"A cow," said Ron, nodding. "But Ron's not that down-to-earth. He's a Curse-Breaker, isn't he, he likes a bit of adventure, a bit of glamour... I expect that's why he's gone for Phlegm."
"Stop calling her that, Ron," said Mrs. Weasley sharply, as Ron and Ron laughed. "Well, I'd better get on... Eat your eggs while they're warm, Ron."
Looking careworn, she left the room. Ron still seemed slightly punch-drunk; he was shaking his head experimentally like a dog trying to rid its ears of water.
"Don't you get used to her if she's staying in the same house?" Ron asked.
"Well, you do," said Ron, "but if she jumps out at you unexpectedly, like then..."
"It's pathetic," said Ron furiously, striding away from Ron as far as she could go and turning to face him with her arms folded once she had reached the wall.
"You don't really want her around forever?" Ron asked Ron incredulously. When he merely shrugged, she said, "Well, Mum's going to put a stop to it if she can, I bet you anything."
"How's she going to manage that?" asked Ron.
"She keeps trying to get Weasley round for dinner. I think she's hoping Ron will fall for Weasley instead. I hope he does, I'd much rather have her in the family."
"Yeah, that'll work," said Ron sarcastically. "Listen, no bloke in his right mind's going to fancy Weasley when Ron's around. I mean, Weasley is okay-looking when she isn't doing stupid things to her hair and her nose, but..."
"She's a damn sight nicer than Phlegm? said Ron.
"And she's more intelligent, she's an Auror!" said Ron from the corner.
"Ron's not stupid, she was good enough to enter the Triwizard Tournament," said Ron.
"Not you as well!" said Ron bitterly.
"I suppose you like the way Phlegm says ' 'Any,' do you?" asked Ron scornfully.
"No," said Ron, wishing he hadn't spoken, "I was just saying, Phlegm... I mean, Ron..."
"I'd much rather have Weasley in the family," said Ron. "At least she's a laugh."
"She hasn't been much of a laugh lately," said Ron. "Every time I've seen her she's looked more like Moaning Ron."
"That's not fair," snapped Ron. "She still hasn't got over what happened... you know... I mean, he was her cousin!"
Ron's heart sank. They had arrived at Ron. He picked up a fork and began shoveling scrambled eggs into his mouth, hoping to deflect any invitation to join in this part of the conversation.
"Weasley and Ron barely knew each other!" said Ron. "Ron was in Azkaban half her life and before that their families never met..."
"That's not the point," said Ron. "She thinks it was her limit he died!"
"How does she work that one out?" asked Ron, in spite of himself.
"Well, she was fighting Weasleyatrix Weasley, wasn't she? I think she feels that if only she had finished her off, Weasleyatrix couldn't have killed Ron."
"That's stupid," said Ron.
"It's survivor's guilt," said Ron. "I know Weasley's tried to talk her round, but she's still really down. She's actually having trouble with her Metamorphosing!"
"With her...?"
"She can't change her appearance like she used to," explained Ron. "I think her powers must have been affected by shock, or something."
"I didn't know that could happen," said Ron.
"Nor did I," said Ron, "but I suppose if you're really depressed..."
The door opened again and Mrs. Weasley popped her head in. "Ron," she whispered, "come downstairs and help me with the lunch."
"I'm talking to this lot!" said Ron, outraged.
"Now!" said Mrs. Weasley, and withdrew.
"She only wants me there so she doesn't have to be alone with Phlegm!" said Ron crossly. She swung her long red hair around in a very good imitation of Ron and pranced across the room with her arms held aloft like a ballerina.
"You lot had better come down quickly too," she said as she left.
Ron took advantage of the temporary silence to eat more breakfast. Ron was peering into Ron and Ron's boxes, though every now and then she cast sideways looks at Ron. Ron, who was now helping himself to Ron...s toast, was still gazing dreamily at the door.
"What's this?" Ron asked eventually, holding up what looked like a small telescope.
"Dunno," said Ron, "but if Ron and Ron left it here, it's probably not ready for the joke shop yet, so be careful"
"Your mum said the shop's going well," said Ron. "Said Ron and Ron have got a real flair for business."
"That's an understatement," said Ron. "They're raking in the Galleons! I can't wait to see the place, we haven't been to Diagon Alley yet, because Mum says Dad's got to be there for extra security and he's been really busy at work, but it sounds excellent."
"And what about Ron?" asked Ron; the third-eldest Weasley brother had fallen out with the rest of the family. "Is he talking to your mum and dad again?"
"Nope," said Ron.
"But he knows your dad was right all along now about Weasley being back..."
"Weasley says people find it far easier to forgive others for being wrong than being right," said Ron. "I heard him telling your mum, Ron."
"Sounds like the sort of mental thing Weasley would say," said Ron.
"He's going to be giving me private lessons this year," said Ron conversationally.
Ron choked on his bit of toast, and Ron gasped.
"You kept that quiet!" said Ron.
"I only just remembered," said Ron honestly. "He told me last night in your broom shed."
"Blimey... private lessons with Weasley!" said Ron, looking impressed. "I wonder why he's... ?"
His voice tailed away. Ron saw him and Ron exchange looks. Ron laid down his knife and fork, his heart beating rather fast considering that all he was doing was sitting in bed. Weasley had said to do it... Why not now? He fixed his eyes on his fork, which was gleaming in the sunlight streaming into his lap, and said, "I don't know exactly why he's going to be giving me lessons, but I think it must be because of the prophecy."
Neither Ron nor Ron spoke. Ron had the impression that both had frozen. He continued, still speaking to his fork, "You know, the one they were trying to steal at the Ministry."
"Nobody knows what it said, though," said Ron quickly. "It got smashed."
"Although the Prophet says..." began Ron, but Ron said, "Shh!"
"The Prophet's got it right," said Ron, looking up at them both with a great effort: Ron seemed frightened and Ron amazed. "That glass ball that smashed wasn't the only record of the prophecy. I heard the whole thing in Weasley's office, he was the one the prophecy was made to, so he could tell me. From what it said," Ron took a deep breath, "it looks like I'm the one who's got to finish off Weasley... At least, it said neither of us could live while the other survives."
The three of them gazed at one another in silence for a moment. Then there was a loud bang and Ron vanished behind a puff of black smoke.
"Ron!" shouted Ron and Ron; the breakfast tray slid to the floor with a crash.
Ron emerged, coughing, out of the smoke, clutching the telescope and sporting a brilliantly purple black eye.
"I squeezed it and it... it punched me!" she gasped.
And sure enough, they now saw a tiny fist on a long spring protruding from the end of the telescope.
"Don't worry," said Ron, who was plainly trying not to laugh, "Mum'll fix that, she's good at healing minor injuries..."
"Oh well, never mind that now!" said Ron hastily. "Ron, oh, Ron..."
She sat down on the edge of his bed again.
"We wondered, after we got back from the Ministry... Obviously, we didn't want to say anything to you, but from what Ron Weasley said about the prophecy, how it was about you and Weasley, well, we thought it might be something like this... Oh, Ron..." She stared at him, then whispered, "Are you scared?"
"Not as much as I was," said Ron. "When I first heard it, I was... but now, it seems as though I always knew I'd have to face him in the end..."
"When we heard Weasley was collecting you in person, we thought he might be telling you something or showing you something to do with the prophecy," said Ron eagerly. "And we were kind of right, weren't we? He wouldn't be giving you lessons if he thought you were a goner, wouldn't waste his time... he must think you've got a chance!"
"That's true," said Ron. "I wonder what he'll teach you, Ron? Really advanced defensive magic, probably... powerful countercurses... anti-jinxes..."
Ron did not really listen. A warmth was spreading through him that had nothing to do with the sunlight; a tight obstruction in his chest seemed to be dissolving. He knew that Ron and Ron were more shocked than they were letting on, but the mere fact that they were still there on either side of him, speaking bracing words of comfort, not shrinking from him as though he were contaminated or dangerous, was worth more than he could ever tell them.
"...and evasive enchantments generally," concluded Ron. "Well, at least you know one lesson you'll be having this year, that's one more than Ron and me. I wonder when our OWL results will come?"
"Cant be long now, it's been a month," said Ron.
"Hang on," said Ron, as another part of last night's conversation came back to him. "I think Weasley said our OWL results would be arriving today!"
"Today?" shrieked Ron. "Today? But why didn't you... oh my God... you should have said..."
She leapt to her feet.
"I'm going to see whether any owls have come..."
But when Ron arrived downstairs ten minutes later, fully dressed and carrying his empty breakfast tray, it was to find Ron sitting at the
kitchen table in great agitation, while Mrs. Weasley tried to lessen her resemblance to half a panda.
"It just won't budge," Mrs. Weasley was saying anxiously, standing over Ron with her wand in her hand and a copy of The Healer's Helpmate open at "Bruises, Cuts, and Abrasions." "This has always worked before, I just can't understand it."
"It'll be Ron and Ron's idea of a funny joke, making sure it can't come off," said Ron.
"But it's got to come off!" squeaked Ron. "I can't go around looking like this forever!"
"You won't, dear, we'll find an antidote, don't worry," said Mrs. Weasley soothingly.
"Ron told me W Ron and Ron are very amusing!" said Ron, smiling serenely.
"Yes, I can hardly breathe for laughing," snapped Ron.
She jumped up and started walking round and round the kitchen, twisting her fingers together.
"Mrs. Weasley, you're quite, quite sure no owls have arrived this morning?"
"Yes, dear, I'd have noticed," said Mrs. Weasley patiently. "But it's barely nine, there's still plenty of time..."
"I know I messed up Ancient Runes," muttered Ron feverishly, "I definitely made at least one serious mistranslation. And the Defense Against the Dark Arts practical was no good at all. I thought Transfiguration went all right at the time, but looking back..."
"Ron, will you shut up, you're not the only one who's nervous!" barked Ron. "And when you've got your eleven 'Outstanding OWLs...’"
"Don't, don't, don't!" said Ron, flapping her hands hysterically. "I know I've failed everything!"
"What happens if we fail?" Ron asked the room at large, but it was again Ron who answered.
"We discuss our options with our Head of House, I asked Professor Weasley at the end of last term."
Ron's stomach squirmed. He wished he had eaten less breakfast.
"At Beauxbatons," said Ron complacently, "we 'ad a different way of doing things. I think eet was better. We sat our examinations after six years of study, not five, and then..."
Ron's words were drowned in a scream. Ron was pointing through the kitchen window. Three black specks were clearly visible in the sky, growing larger all the time.
"They're definitely owls," said Ron hoarsely, jumping up to join Ron at the window.
"And there are three of them," said Ron, hastening to her other side.
"One for each of us," said Ron in a terrified whisper. "Oh no... oh no... oh no..."
She gripped both Ron and Ron tightly around the elbows.
The owls were flying directly at the Burrow, three handsome tawnies, each of which, it became clear as they flew lower over the path leading up to the house, was carrying a large square envelope.
"Oh no!" squealed Ron.
Mrs. Weasley squeezed past them and opened the kitchen window. One, two, three, the owls soared through it and landed on the table in a neat line. All three of them lifted their right legs.
Ron moved forward. The letter addressed to him was tied to the leg of the owl in the middle. He untied it with fumbling fingers. To his left, Ron
was trying to detach his own results; to his right, Ron's hands were shaking so much she was making her whole owl tremble.
Nobody in the kitchen spoke. At last, Ron managed to detach the envelope. He slit it open quickly and unfolded the parchment inside.
Ordinary Wizarding Level Results
Pass Grades:
Outstanding (O)
Exceeds Expectations (E)
Acceptable (A)
Fail Grades:
Poor (P)
Dreadful (D)
Troll (T)
Ron Ron Weasley has achieved:
Astronomy A
Care of Magical Creatures E
Charms E
Defense Against the Dark Arts O
Divination P
Herbology E
History of Magic D
Potions E
Transfiguration E
Ron read the parchment through several times, his breathing becoming easier with each reading. It was all right: He had always known that he would fail Divination, and he had had no chance of passing History of Magic, given that he had collapsed halfway through the examination, but he had passed everything else! He ran his finger down the grades... he had passed well in Transfiguration and Herbology, he had even exceeded
expectations at Potions! And best of all, he had achieved "Outstanding" at Defense Against the Dark Arts!
He looked around. Ron had her back to him and her head bent, but Ron was looking delighted.
"Only failed Divination and History of Magic, and who cares about them?" he said happily to Ron. "Here... swap..."
Ron glanced down Ron's grades: There were no "Outstandings" there...
"Knew you'd be top at Defense Against the Dark Arts," said Ron, punching Ron on the shoulder. "We've done all right, haven't we?"
"Well done!" said Mrs. Weasley proudly, ruffling Ron's hair. "Seven OWLs, that's more than Ron and Ron got together!"
"Ron?" said Ron tentatively, for Ron still hadn't turned around. "How did you do?"
"I--not bad," said Ron in a small voice.
"Oh, come off it," said Ron, striding over to her and whipping her results out of her hand. "Yep... ten 'Outstandings' and one 'Exceeds Expectations' at Defense Against the Dark Arts." He looked down at her, half-amused, half-exasperated. "You're actually disappointed, aren't you?"
Ron shook her head, but Ron laughed.
"Well, we're N.E.W.T. students now!" grinned Ron. "Mum, are there any more sausages?"
Ron looked back down at his results. They were as good as he could have hoped for. He felt just one tiny twinge of regret... This was the end of his ambition to become an Auror. He had not secured the required Potions grade. He had known all along that he wouldn't, but he still felt a sinking in his stomach as he looked again at that small black E.
It was odd, really, seeing that it had been a Death Eater in disguise who had first told Ron he would make a good Auror, but somehow the idea had taken hold of him, and he couldn't really think of anything else he would like to be. Moreover, it had seemed the right destiny for him since he had heard the prophecy a few weeks ago... Neither can live while the other survives...Wouldn't he be living up to the prophecy, and giving himself the best chance of survival, if he joined those highly trained wizards whose job it was to find and kill Weasley?
Chapter 6: Ron's Detour
Ron remained within the confines of the Burrow's garden over the next few weeks. He spent most of his days playing two-a-side Quidditch in the Weasleys' orchard (he and Ron against Ron and Ron; Ron was dreadful and Ron good, so they were reasonably well matched) and his evenings eating triple helpings of everything Mrs. Weasley put in front of him.
It would have been a happy, peaceful holiday had it not been for the stones of disappearances, odd accidents, even of deaths now appearing almost daily in the Prophet. Sometimes Ron and Mr. Weasley brought home news before it even reached the paper. To Mrs. Weasley’s displeasure, Ron's sixteenth birthday celebrations were marred by grisly tidings brought to the party by Ron Weasley, who was looking gaunt and grim, his brown hair streaked liberally with gray, his clothes more ragged and patched than ever.
"There have been another couple of dementor attacks," he announced, as Mrs. Weasley passed him a large slice of birthday cake. "And they've found Ron Weasley's body in a shack up north. The Dark Mark had been set over it... well, frankly, I'm surprised he stayed alive for even a year after deserting the Death Eaters; Ron's brother, Ron, only managed a few days as far as I can remember."
"Yes, well," said Mrs. Weasley, frowning, "perhaps we should talk about something diff..."
"Did you hear about Ron Weasley, Ron?" asked Ron, who was being plied with wine by Ron. "The man who ran..."
"Is the ice-cream place in Diagon Alley?" Ron interrupted, with an unpleasant, hollow sensation in the pit of his stomach. "He used to give me free ice creams. What's happened to him?"
"Dragged off, by the look of his place."
"Why?" asked Ron, while Mrs. Weasley pointedly glared at Ron.
"Who knows? He must've upset them somehow. He was a good man, Ron."
"Talking of Diagon Alley," said Mr. Weasley, "looks like Weasley's gone too."
"The wandmaker?" said Ron, looking startled.
"That's the one. Shop's empty. No sign of a struggle. No one knows whether he left voluntarily or was kidnapped."
"But what'll people do for wands?"
"They'll make do with other makers," said Weasley. "But Weasley was the best, and if the other side have got him it's not so good for us."
The day after this rather gloomy birthday tea, their letters and booklists arrived from Hogwarts. Ron's included a surprise: he had been made Quidditch Captain.
"That gives you equal status with prefects!" cried Ron happily. "You can use our special bathroom now and everything!"
"Wow, I remember when Ron wore one of these," said Ron, examining the badge with glee. "Ron, this is so cool, you're my Captain... if you let me back on the team, I suppose, ha ha..."
"Well, I don't suppose we can put off a trip to Diagon Alley much longer now you've got these," sighed Mrs. Weasley, looking down Ron...s booklist. "We'll go on Saturday as long as your father doesn't have to go into work again. I'm not going there without him."
"Mum, d'you honestly think You-Know-Who's going to be hiding behind a bookshelf in Flourish and Blotts?" sniggered Ron.
"Weasley and Weasley went on holiday, did they?" said Mrs. Weasley, firing up at once. "If you think security's a laughing matter you can stay behind and I'll get your things myself..."
"No, I wanna come, I want to see Ron and Ron's shop!" said Ron hastily.
"Then you just buck up your ideas, young man, before I decide you're too immature to come with us!" said Mrs. Weasley angrily, snatching up her clock, all nine hands of which were still pointing at "mortal peril," and balancing it on top of a pile of just-laundered towels. "And that goes for returning to Hogwarts as well!"
Ron turned to stare incredulously at Ron as his mother hoisted the laundry basket and the teetering clock into her arms and stormed out of the room.
"Blimey... you can't even make a joke round here anymore..."
But Ron was careful not to be flippant about Weasley over the next few days. Saturday dawned without any more outbursts from Mrs. Weasley, though she seemed very tense at breakfast. Ron, who would be staying at home with Ron (much to Ron and Ron's pleasure), passed a full money bag across the table to Ron.
"Where's mine?" demanded Ron at once, his eyes wide.
"That's already Ron's, idiot," said Ron. "I got it out of your vault for you, Ron, because it's taking about five hours for the public to get to their gold at the moment, the goblins have tightened security so much. Two days ago
Arkie Philpott had a Probity Probe stuck up his... Well, trust me, this way's easier."
"Thanks, Ron," said Ron, pocketing his gold.
"E is always so thoughtful," purred Ron adoringly, stroking Ron's nose. Ron mimed vomiting into her cereal behind Ron. Ron choked over his cornflakes, and Ron thumped him on the back.
It was an overcast, murky day. One of the special Ministry of Magic cars, in which Ron had ridden once before, was awaiting them in the front yard when they emerged from the house, pulling on their cloaks.
"It's good Dad can get us these again," said Ron appreciatively, stretching luxuriously as the car moved smoothly away from the Burrow, Ron and Ron waving from the kitchen window. He, Ron, Ron, and Ron were all sitting in roomy comfort in the wide backseat.
"Don't get used to it, it's only because of Ron," said Mr. Weasley over his shoulder. He and Mrs. Weasley were in front with the Ministry driver; the front passenger seat had obligingly stretched into what resembled a two-seater sofa. "He's been given top-grade security status. And we'll be joining up with additional security at the Leaky Cauldron too."
Ron said nothing; he did not much fancy doing his shopping while surrounded by a battalion of Aurors. He had stowed his Invisibility Cloak in his backpack and felt that, if that was good enough for Weasley, it ought
to be good enough for the Ministry, though now he came to think of it, he was not sure the Ministry knew about his cloak.
"Here you are, then," said the driver, a surprisingly short while later, speaking for the first time as he slowed in Charing Cross Road and stopped outside the Leaky Cauldron. "I'm to wait for you, any idea how long you'll be?"
"A couple of hours, I expect," said Mr. Weasley. "Ah, good, he's here!"
Ron imitated Mr. Weasley and peered through the window; his heart leapt. There were no Aurors waiting outside the inn, but instead the gigantic, black-bearded form of Ron Weasley, the Hogwarts gamekeeper, wearing a long beaverskin coat, beaming at the sight of Ron's face and oblivious to the startled stares of passing Muggles.
"Ron!" he boomed, sweeping Ron into a bone-crushing hug the moment Ron had stepped out of the car. "Ron... Witherwings, I mean... yeh should see him, Ron, he's so happy ter be back in the open air..."
"Glad he's pleased," said Ron, grinning as he massaged his ribs. "We didn't know 'security' meant you!"
"I know, jus' like old times, innit? See, the Ministry wanted ter send a bunch o' Aurors, but Weasley said I'd do," said Weasley proudly, throwing
out his chest and tucking his thumbs into his pockets. "Lets get goin' then... after yeh, Ron, Ron..."
The Leaky Cauldron was, for the first time in Ron's memory, completely empty. Only Ron the landlord, wizened and toothless, remained of the old crowd. He looked up hopefully as they entered, but before he could speak, Weasley said importantly, "Jus' passin' through today, Ron, sure yeh understand, Hogwarts business, yeh know."
Ron nodded gloomily and returned to wiping glasses; Ron, Ron, Weasley, and the Weasleys walked through the bar and out into the chilly little courtyard at the back where the dustbins stood. Weasley raised his pink umbrella and rapped a certain brick in the wall, which opened at once to form an archway onto a winding cobbled street. They stepped through the entrance and paused, looking around.
Diagon Alley had changed. The colorful, glittering window displays of spellbooks, potion ingredients, and cauldrons were lost to view, hidden behind the large Ministry of Magic posters that had been pasted over them. Most of these somber purple posters carried blown-up versions of the security advice on the Ministry pamphlets that had been sent out over the summer, but others bore moving black-and-white photographs of Death Eaters known to be on the loose. Weasleyatrix Weasley was sneering from the front of the nearest apothecary. A few windows were boarded up, including those of Ron Weasley's Ice Cream Parlor. On the other hand, a number of shabby-looking stalls had sprung up along the street. The nearest one,
which had been erected outside Flourish and Blotts, under a striped, stained awning, had a cardboard sign pinned to its front:
AMULETS
Effective Against Werewolves, Dementors, and Inferi!
A seedy-looking little wizard was rattling armfuls of silver symbols on chains at passersby.
"One for your little girl, madam?" he called at Mrs. Weasley as they passed, leering at Ron. "Protect her pretty neck?"
"If I were on duty..." said Mr. Weasley, glaring angrily at the amulet seller.
"Yes, but don't go arresting anyone now, dear, we're in a hurry," said Mrs. Weasley, nervously consulting a list. "I think we'd better do Ron Weasley's first, Ron wants new dress robes, and Ron's showing much too much ankle in his school robes, and you must need new ones too, Ron, you've grown so much... come on, everyone..."
"Ron, it doesn't make sense for all of us to go to Ron Weasley's," said Mr. Weasley. "Why don't those three go with Weasley, and we can go to Flourish and Blotts and get everyone's school-books?"
"I don't know," said Mrs. Weasley anxiously, clearly torn between a desire to finish the shopping quickly and the wish to stick together in a pack. "Weasley, do you think...- ?"
"Don't fret, they'll be fine with me, Ron," said Weasley soothingly, waving an airy hand the size of a dustbin lid. Mrs. Weasley did not look entirely convinced, but allowed the separation, scurrying off toward Flourish and Blotts with her husband and Ron while Ron, Ron, Ron, and Weasley set off for Ron Weasley's.
Ron noticed that many of the people who passed them had the same harried, anxious look as Mrs. Weasley, and that nobody was stopping to talk anymore; the shoppers stayed together in their own tightly knit groups, moving intently about their business. Nobody seemed to be shopping alone.
"Migh' be a bit of a squeeze in there with all of us," said Weasley, stopping outside Ron Weasley's and bending down to peer through the window. "I'll stand guard outside, all right?"
So Ron, Ron, and Ron entered the little shop together. It appeared, at first glance, to be empty, but no sooner had the door swung shut behind them than they heard a familiar voice issuing from behind a rack of dress robes in spangled green and blue.
"... not a child, in case you haven't noticed, Mother. I am perfectly capable of doing my shopping alone."
There was a clucking noise and a voice Ron recognized as that of Ron Weasley, the owner, said, "Now, dear, your mother's quite right, none of us is supposed to go wandering around on our own anymore, it's nothing to do with being a child..."
"Watch where you're sticking that pin, will you!"
A teenage boy with a pale, pointed face and white-blond hair appeared from behind the rack, wearing a handsome set of dark green robes that glittered with pins around the hem and the edges of the sleeves. He strode to the mirror and examined himself; it was a few moments before he noticed Ron, Ron, and Ron reflected over his shoulder. His light gray eyes narrowed.
"If you're wondering what the smell is, Mother, a Mudblood just walked in," said Ron Weasley.
"I don't think there's any need for language like that!" said Ron Weasley, scurrying out from behind the clothes rack holding a tape measure and a wand. "And I don't want wands drawn in my shop either!" she added hastily, for a glance toward the door had shown her Ron and Ron both standing there with their wands out and pointing at Weasley. Ron, who was standing slightly behind them, whispered, "No, don't, honestly, it's not worth it. "
"Yeah, like you'd dare do magic out of school," sneered Weasley. "Who blacked your eye, Weasley? I want to send them flowers."
"That's quite enough!" said Ron Weasley sharply, looking over her shoulder for support. "Ron, please!"
Ron Weasley strolled out from behind the clothes rack.
"Put those away," she said coldly to Ron and Ron. "If you at-tack my son again, I shall ensure that it is the last thing you ever do."
"Really?" said Ron, taking a step forward and gazing into the smoothly arrogant face that, for all its pallor, still resembled her sister's. He was as tall as she was now. "Going to get a few Death Eater pals to do us in, are you?"
Ron Weasley squealed and clutched at her heart.
"Really, you shouldn't accuse... dangerous thing to say... wands away, please!"
But Ron did not lower his wand. Ron Weasley smiled unpleasantly.
"I see that being Weasley's favorite has given you a false sense of security, Ron Weasley. But Weasley won't always be there to protect you."
Ron looked mockingly all around the shop. "Wow... look at that... he's not here now! So why not have a go? They might be able to find you a double cell in Azkaban with your loser of a husband!"
Weasley made an angry movement toward Ron, but stumbled over his overlong robe. Ron laughed loudly.
"Don't you dare talk to my mother like that, Weasley!" Weasley snarled.
"It's all right, Ron," said Ron, restraining him with her thin white fingers upon his shoulder. "I expect Weasley will be reunited with dear Ron before I am reunited with Ron."
Ron raised his wand higher.
"Ron, no!" moaned Ron, grabbing his arm and attempting to push it down by his side. "Think... You mustn't... You'll be in such trouble..."
Ron Weasley dithered for a moment on the spot, then seemed to decide to act as though nothing was happening in the hope that it wouldn't. She bent toward Weasley, who was still glaring at Ron.
"I think this left sleeve could come up a little bit more, dear, let me just..."
"Ouch!" bellowed Weasley, slapping her hand away. "Watch where you're putting your pins, woman! Mother, I don't think I want these anymore."
He pulled the robes over his head and threw them onto the floor at Ron Weasley's feet.
"You're right, Ron," said Ron, with a contemptuous glance at Ron, "now I know the kind of scum that shops here... We'll do better at Twilfitt and Tatting's."
And with that, the pair of them strode out of the shop, Weasley taking care to bang as hard as he could into Ron on the way out.
"Well, really? said Ron Weasley, snatching up the fallen robes and moving the tip of her wand over them like a vacuum cleaner, so that it removed all the dust.
She was distracted all through the fitting of Ron's and Ron's new robes, tried to sell Ron wizard's dress robes instead of witch's, and when she finally bowed them out of the shop it was with an air of being glad to see the back of them.
"Got ev'rything?" asked Weasley brightly when they reappeared at his side.
"Just about," said Ron. "Did you see the Weasleys?"
"Yeah," said Weasley, unconcerned. "Bu they wouldn... dare make trouble in the middle o' Diagon Alley, Ron. Don' worry abou1 them."
Ron, Ron, and Ron exchanged looks, but before they could disabuse Weasley of this comfortable notion, Mr. and Mrs. Weasley and Ron appeared, all clutching heavy packages of books.
"Everyone all right?" said Mrs. Weasley. "Got your robes? Right then, we can pop in at the Apothecary and Eeylops on the way to Ron and Ron's... stick close, now..."
Neither Ron nor Ron bought any ingredients at the Apothecary, seeing that they were no longer studying Potions, but both bought large boxes of owl nuts for Ron and Ron at Eeylops Owl Emporium. Then, with Mrs. Weasley checking her watch every minute or so, they headed farther along the street in search of Weasleys' Wizard Wheezes, the joke shop run by Ron and Ron.
"We really haven't got too long," Mrs. Weasley said. "So we'll just have a quick look around and then back to the car. We must be close, that's number ninety-two... ninety-four..."
"Whoa,"said Ron, stopping in his tracks.
Set against the dull, poster-muffled shop Fronts around them, Ron and Rons windows hit the eye like a firework display. Casual passersby were looking back over their shoulders at the windows, and a few rather stunned-looking people had actually come to a halt, transfixed. The left-hand window was dazzlingly full of an assortment of goods that revolved, popped, flashed, bounced, and shrieked; Rons eyes began to water just looking at it. The right-hand window was covered with a gigantic poster, purple like those of the Ministry, but emblazoned with flashing yellow letters:
WHY ARE YOU WORRYING ABOUT
YOU-KNOW-WHO?
YOU SHOULD BE WORRYING ABOUT
U-NO-POO--
THE CONSTIPATION SENSATION
THAT'S GRIPPING THE NATION!
Ron started to laugh. He heard a weak sort of moan beside him and looked around to see Mrs. Weasley gazing, dumbfounded, at the poster. Her lips moved silently, mouthing the name "U-No-Poo."
"They'll be murdered in their beds!" she whispered.
"No they won’t!" said Ron, who, like Ron, was laughing. "This is brilliant!"
And he and Ron led the way into the shop. It was packed with customers; Ron could not get near the shelves. He stared around, looking up at the boxes piled to the ceiling: Here were the Skiving Snackboxes that the twins had perfected during their last, unfinished year at Hogwarts; Ron noticed that the Nosebleed Nougat was most popular, with only one battered box left on the shelf. There were bins full of trick wands, the cheapest merely turning into rubber chickens or pairs of briefs when waved, the most expensive beating the unwary user around the head and neck, and boxes of quills, which came in Self-Inking, Spell-Checking, and Smart-Answer varieties. A space cleared in the crowd, and Ron pushed his way toward the counter, where a gaggle of delighted ten-year-olds was watching a tiny little wooden man slowly ascending the steps to a real set of gallows, both perched on a box that read: Reusable hangman - spell it or he'll swing!
"Patented Daydream Charms"
Ron had managed to squeeze through to a large display near the counter and was reading the information on the back of a box bearing a highly colored picture of a handsome youth and a swooning girl who were standing on the deck of a pirate ship.
"One simple incantation and you will enter a top-quality, highly realistic, thirty-minute daydream, easy to fit into the average school lesson and virtually undetectable (side effects include vacant expression and minor drooling). Not for sale to under-sixteens. You know," said Ron, looking up at Ron, "that really is extraordinary magic!"
"For that, Ron," said a voice behind them, "you can have one for free."
A beaming Ron stood before them, wearing a set of magenta robes that clashed magnificently with his flaming hair.
"How are you, Ron?" They shook hands. "And what's happened to your eye, Ron?"
Your punching telescope," she said ruefully.
"Oh blimey, I forgot about those," said Ron. "Here..."
He pulled a tub out of his pocket and handed it to her; she unscrewed it gingerly to reveal a thick yellow paste.
"Just dab it on, that bruise'll be gone within the hour," said Ron. "We had to find a decent bruise remover. We're testing most of our products on ourselves."
Ron looked nervous. "It is safe, isn't it?" she asked.
"Course it is," said Ron bracingly. "Come on, Ron, I'll give you a tour."
Ron left Ron dabbing her black eye with paste and followed Ron toward the back of the shop, where he saw a stand of card and rope tricks.
"Muggle magic tricks!" said Ron happily, pointing them out. "For freaks like Dad, you know, who love Muggle stuff. It's not a big earner, but we do fairly steady business, they're great novelties... Oh, here's Ron..."
Ron's twin shook Rons hand energetically.
"Giving him the tour? Come through the back, Ron, that's where we're making the real money...pocket anything, you, and you'll pay in more than Galleons!" he added warningly to a small boy who hastily whipped his hand out of the tub labeled:
EDIBLE DARK MARKS----THEY'LL MAKE ANYONE SICK!
Ron pushed back a curtain beside the Muggle tricks and Ron saw a darker, less crowded room. The packaging on the products lining these shelves was more subdued.
"We've just developed this more serious line," said Ron. "Funny how it happened..."
"You wouldn't believe how many people, even people who work at the Ministry, can't do a decent Shield Charm," said Ron. "'Course, they didn't have you teaching them, Ron."
"That's right... Well, we thought Shield Hats were a bit of a laugh, you know, challenge your mate to jinx you while wearing it and watch his face when the jinx just bounces off. But the Ministry bought five hundred for all its support staff! And we're still getting massive orders!"
"So we've expanded into a range of Shield Cloaks, Shield Gloves..."
"... I mean, they wouldn't help much against the Unforgivable Curses, but for minor to moderate hexes or jinxes..."
"And then we thought we'd get into the whole area of Defense Against the Dark Arts, because it's such a money spinner," continued Ron enthusiastically. "This is cool. Look, Instant Darkness Powder, we're importing it from Peru. Handy if you want to make a quick escape."
"And our Decoy Detonators are just walking off the shelves, look," said Ron, pointing at a number of weird-looking black horn-type objects that were indeed attempting to scurry out of sight. "You just drop one surreptitiously and it'll run off and make a nice loud noise out of sight, giving you a diversion if you need one.
"Handy," said Ron, impressed.
"Here," said Ron, catching a couple and throwing them to Ron.
A young witch with short blonde hair poked her head around the curtain; Ron saw that she too was wearing magenta staff robes.
"There's a customer out here looking for a joke cauldron, Mr. Weasley and Mr. Weasley," she said.
Ron found it very odd to hear Ron and Ron called "Mr. Weasley," but they took it in their stride.
"Right you are, Verity, I'm coming," said Ron promptly. "Ron, you help yourself to anything you want, all right? No charge."
"I can't do that!" said Ron, who had already pulled out his money bag to pay for the Decoy Detonators.
"You don't pay here," said Ron firmly, waving away Ron's gold.
"But..."
"You gave us our start-up loan, we haven't forgotten," said Ron sternly "Take whatever you like, and just remember to tell people where you got it, if they ask."
Ron swept off through the curtain to help with the customers, and Ron led Ron back into the main part of the shop to find Ron and Ron still poring over the Patented Daydream Charms.
"Haven't you girls found our special WonderWitch products yet?" asked Ron. "Follow me, ladies..."
Near the window was an array of violently pink products around which a cluster of excited girls was giggling enthusiastically. Ron and Ron both hung back, looking wary.
"There you go," said Ron proudly. "Best range of love potions you'll find anywhere."
Ron raised an eyebrow skeptically. "Do they work?" she asked.
"Certainly they work, for up to twenty-four hours at a time depending on the weight of the boy in question..."
"... and the attractiveness of the girl," said Ron, reappearing suddenly at their side. "But we're not selling them to our sister," he added, becoming
suddenly stern, "not when she's already got about five boys on the go from what we've..."
"Whatever you've heard from Ron is a big fat lie," said Ron calmly, leaning forward to take a small pink pot off the shelf. "What's this?"
"Guaranteed ten-second pimple vanisher," said Ron. "Excellent on everything from boils to blackheads, but don't change the subject. Are you or are you not currently going out with a boy called Ron Ron?"
"Yes, I am," said Ron. "And last time I looked, he was definitely one boy, not five. What are those?"
She was pointing at a number of round balls of fluff in shades of pink and purple, all rolling around the bottom of a cage and emitting high-pitched squeaks.
"Pygmy Puffs," said Ron. "Miniature puffskeins, we can...t breed them fast enough. So what about Ron Weasley?"
"I dumped him, he was a bad loser," said Ron, putting a finger through the bars of the cage and watching the Pygmy Puffs crowd around it. "They're really cute!"
"They're fairly cuddly, yes," conceded Ron. "But you're moving through boyfriends a bit fast, aren't you?"
Ron turned to look at him, her hands on her hips. There was such a Mrs. Weasley-ish glare on her face that Ron was surprised Ron didn't recoil.
"It's none of your business. And I'll thank you'' she added angrily to Ron, who had just appeared at Ron's elbow, laden with merchandise, "not to tell tales about me to these two!"
"That's three Galleons, nine Sickles, and a Knut," said Ron, examining the many boxes in Ron's arms. "Cough up."
"I'm your brother!"
